## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The nonlinearity can appear in restoring force terms, damping terms, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced cubic oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear with periodic forcing)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Mathieu-type oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametric excitation)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * v (Duffing + van der Pol combined)
- Softening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t + c5) (general driven Duffing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial terms in x
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection; sign determines damping vs. anti-damping
- Products like v*x² indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type self-excited oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates external periodic driving force
- Parametric excitation appears as time-dependent coefficients multiplying position: f(t)*x rather than additive f(t)
- Conservation of energy (no v or t dependence) implies dv_dt = -dU/dx, a pure potential gradient
- Negative cubic coefficient (x - x³) indicates double-well potential; positive (x + x³) indicates hardening spring
- Phase-space structure: if dv_dt depends only on x, trajectories in (x,v) space are closed curves (conservative system)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0586*v³ - 0.7167*v - 0.3583*v*exp(-|v|) + 0.6686*sin(t)`

Key features of the GT:
1. A `v³` term
2. A `v` term
3. A `v*exp(-|v|)` term
4. A `sin(t)` term

The critical challenge is the `v*exp(-|v|)` term. Note that `|v|` is not differentiable and involves absolute value, which is hard to represent with simple expressions.

Let me check candidates that have exponential terms involving `v`:

**Candidate 1:** Has `v*exp(c6*v²)` - This is `v*exp(c6*v²)`. Note that `-|v| = -√(v²)`, but `c6*v²` is not the same as `-|v|`. For `v² > 0`, `exp(-|v|) ≠ exp(c*v²)` for any constant c. These are fundamentally different functions. **No match.**

**Candidate 3:** Same structure as relevant part of 1: `v*exp(c6*v²)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 4:** Has `v*exp(c6*v²)` and `v*exp(c8*x)`. The x-dependent term doesn't help. **No match.**

**Candidate 15:** Has `exp(c6*v)*sin(c7*t + c8)`. This mixes v-exponential with t-sinusoidal, not the right structure. **No match.**

**Candidate 42:** `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*v + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1) + c9*v⁵`

The `log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1)` term is interesting. Note that for large negative `c8*v`, `log(c7*exp(c8*v) + 1) ≈ c7*exp(c8*v)`, and for large positive `c8*v`, it's approximately `c8*v + log(c7)`. This is a softplus-like function, not `v*exp(-|v|)`. **No match.**

Now let me reconsider. The GT has `sin(t)`, but many candidates use `cos(c2*t + c3)`. Since `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, setting `c2=1, c3=-π/2` works. So `cos(c2*t + c3)` can represent `sin(t)`.

The fundamental issue is that **no candidate contains `v*exp(-|v|)`** or any equivalent form. The `exp(c*v²)` terms in candidates 1, 3, 4 are symmetric in v but have fundamentally different behavior than `exp(-|v|)`.

Let me check if any candidate could approximate the combined effect of `-0.7167*v - 0.3583*v*exp(-|v|)` through other means. Note that `v*exp(-|v|)` behaves like `v` for small `v` and decays for large `|v|`. No polynomial or simple trigonometric/exponential combination can replicate this for all v.

**Candidate 6:** Has `v*exp(c9*v²)` - same issue.

**Candidate 2:** A rational function in v. Could a rational function match `v*exp(-|v|)` for all v? No, because `exp(-|v|)` is not a rational function of v.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-|v|)` or any mechanism to produce the absolute value function inside an exponential. The candidates with `exp(c*v²)` have even symmetry in the exponent (v² is always positive), whereas `|v|` also has even symmetry, but `exp(-|v|)` decays as `exp(-|v|)` while `exp(c*v²)` with c<0 decays as a Gaussian - these are different functional forms that cannot be made equal for all v.

After careful analysis, no candidate can match the GT because none can reproduce the `v*exp(-|v|)` term.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
